        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      William Rodriguez, as founder of the group, was a member of the Families Advisory Council for the
      <a href="/wiki/Lower_Manhattan_Development_Corporation" title="Lower Manhattan Development Corporation">
       Lower Manhattan Development Corporation
      </a>
      (LMDC).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-renewnyc_110-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-renewnyc-110">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        110
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Conferences">
       Conferences
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=9/11_Truth_movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Conferences">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Members of the 9/11 truth organizations, such as 911truth.org and Scholars for 9/11 Truth and Justice, regularly hold meetings and conferences to discuss ongoing research about 9/11 and to strategize about how best to achieve their goals. Many of these conferences are organized by 911truth.org, and some have been covered by the international media.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nationalpost1_111-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-nationalpost1-111">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        111
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Internal_critiques">
       Internal critiques
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=9/11_Truth_movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Internal critiques">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Within the movement, there are alternative theories about what may have happened.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barber_5-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-Barber-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Opponents">
       Opponents
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=9/11_Truth_movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Opponents">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Matt_Taibbi" title="Matt Taibbi">
       Matt Taibbi
      </a>
      of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">
        Rolling Stone
       </a>
      </i>
      assessed that the movement "gives supporters of
      <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">
       Bush
      </a>
      an excuse to dismiss critics of this administration", and expressed concerns about the number of people who believe in 9/11 conspiracy theories.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
       <a href="#cite_note-112">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        112
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">
       Massachusetts Institute of Technology
      </a>
      (MIT) engineering professor
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Thomas_W._Eagar&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Thomas W. Eagar (page does not exist)">
       Thomas W. Eagar
      </a>
      was at first unwilling to acknowledge the concerns of the movement, saying "if (the argument) gets too mainstream, I'll engage in the debate." In response to Steven E. Jones publication of a hypothesis that the World Trade Center was destroyed by controlled demolition, Eagar said that adherents of the 9/11 Truth movement would use the reverse scientific method to arrive at their conclusions, as they "determine what happened, throw out all the data that doesn't fit their conclusion, and then hail their findings as the only possible conclusion".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">
       <a href="#cite_note-113">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        113
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Calling conspiracy theorists "the truthers",
      <a href="/wiki/Bill_Moyers" title="Bill Moyers">
       Bill Moyers
      </a>
      has quoted journalist Robert Parry by stating that the theorists "...threw out all the evidence of al-Qaeda's involvement, from contemporaneous calls from hijack victims on the planes to confessions from al-Qaeda leaders both in and out of captivity that they had indeed done it. Then, recycling some of the right's sophistry techniques, such as using long lists of supposed evidence to overcome the lack of any real evidence, the 'truthers' cherry-picked a few supposed 'anomalies' to build an 'inside-job' story line".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">
       <a href="#cite_note-114">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        114
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al_Qaeda" title="Al Qaeda">
       Al Qaeda
      </a>
      has sharply criticized Iran's ex-president,
      <a href="/wiki/Mahmoud_Ahmadinejad" title="Mahmoud Ahmadinejad">
       Mahmoud Ahmadinejad
      </a>
      , over his suggestions that the U.S. government was behind the September 11 attacks, dismissing his comments as "ridiculous".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">
       <a href="#cite_note-115">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        115
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Some skeptics, who oppose conspiracy as the a-priori explanation to events, and who find most of the questions posed by the Truthers to be either easily answered
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">
       <a href="#cite_note-116">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        116
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      or based on misleading or false facts
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
       <a href="#cite_note-117">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        117
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      have claimed that some of the Truthers are knowingly disseminating false information, with no care for the grieving families, and accordingly called them "disrespectful" or even "sickos".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
       <a href="#cite_note-118">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        118
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Media">
       Media
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=9/11_Truth_movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Media">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Books">
       Books
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=9/11_Truth_movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Books">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      A prominent author of the 9/11 Truth movement literature is theologian
      <a href="/wiki/David_Ray_Griffin" title="David Ray Griffin">
       David Ray Griffin
      </a>
      . His two books,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_New_Pearl_Harbor" title="The New Pearl Harbor">
        The New Pearl Harbor
       </a>
       : Disturbing Questions about the Bush Administration and 9/11
      </i>
      (March 2004), which claimed to outline a methodical, deductive framework for researching 9/11, and
      <i>
       The 9/11 Commission Report: Omissions and Distortions
      </i>
      (October 2004), became best-sellers.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">
       <a href="#cite_note-119">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        119
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Griffin's
      <i>
       Debunking 9/11 Debunking
      </i>
      (May 2007) looks at the way magazines such as
      <i>
       Popular Mechanics
      </i>
      have sought to debunk the alternative 9/11 theories.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
       <a href="#cite_note-120">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        120
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      His 2008 book,
      <i>
       The New Pearl Harbor Revisited: 9/11, the cover-up, and the expos
      </i>
      , was written to update his original book,
      <i>
       The New Pearl Harbor
      </i>
      , reflecting information and insights from five major developments that have occurred since his original publication,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
       <a href="#cite_note-121">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        121
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      while
      <i>
       The Mysterious Collapse of World Trade Center 7: Why the Final Official Report About 9/11 Is Unscientific and False
      </i>
      , published in 2009, examines the credibility of the official investigations into and hypotheses about the destruction of the third skyscraper, WTC 7, focusing on the final official report published in November 2008.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
       <a href="#cite_note-122">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        122
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In September 2004, the interactive "Complete 9/11 Timeline" website by Paul Thompson, a collection of mainstream media reports presented chronologically, was made into the book, entitled
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Terror_Timeline" title="The Terror Timeline">
        The Terror Timeline
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Knight_123-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Knight-123">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        123
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Films">
       Films
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=9/11_Truth_movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Films">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Films made by people associated with the 9/11 Truth movement include:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <i>
        The Great Conspiracy: The 9/11 News Special You Never Saw
       </i>
       (2004) by
       <a href="/wiki/Barrie_Zwicker" title="Barrie Zwicker">
        Barrie Zwicker
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        Martial Law 9/11: Rise of the Police State
       </i>
       (2005) by
       <a href="/wiki/Alex_Jones_(radio_host)" title="Alex Jones (radio host)">
        Alex Jones
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/9/11:_Press_for_Truth" title="9/11: Press for Truth">
         9/11: Press for Truth
        </a>
       </i>
       (2006)
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        911 Mysteries: Demolitions
       </i>
       (2006)
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        9/11: Blueprint for Truth
       </i>
       (2007) and updated
       <i>
        2008 Edition
       </i>
       by Richard Gage
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Loose_Change_(film)" title="Loose Change (film)">
         Loose Change: An American Coup
        </a>
       </i>
       (2009) by
       <a href="/wiki/Dylan_Avery" title="Dylan Avery">
        Dylan Avery
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/New_World_Order_(film)" title="New World Order (film)">
         New World Order
        </a>
       </i>
       (2009) by
       <a href="/wiki/Luke_Meyer" title="Luke Meyer">
        Luke Meyer
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Neel" title="Andrew Neel">
        Andrew Neel
       </a>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Details">
       Details
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=9/11_Truth_movement&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Details">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      These documentaries present a range of alternative theories about how the attacks might have been carried out:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/9/11_Press_for_Truth" title="9/11 Press for Truth">
         9/11 Press for Truth
        </a>
       </i>
       (2006) documents the struggle by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jersey_Widows" title="Jersey Widows">
        Jersey Widows
       </a>
       to open a full investigation of the events, and their frustration while monitoring the 9/11 Commission as part of the
       <a href="/wiki/9/11_Family_Steering_Committee" title="9/11 Family Steering Committee">
        Family Steering Committee
       </a>
       .
      </li>
     </ul>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Alex_Jones_(radio_host)" title="Alex Jones (radio host)">
        Alex Jones
       </a>
       , 9/11 and
       <a href="/wiki/New_World_Order_(conspiracy_theory)" title="New World Order (conspiracy theory)">
        New World Order
       </a>
       conspiracy theorists are the subject of the documentary film
       <a href="/wiki/New_World_Order_(film)" title="New World Order (film)">
        <i>
         New World Order
        </i>
       </a>
       , directed by
       <a href="/wiki/Luke_Meyer" title="Luke Meyer">
        Luke Meyer
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Neel" title="Andrew Neel">
        Andrew Neel
       </a>
       , that debuted on the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Independent_Film_Channel" title="Independent Film Channel">
        Independent Film Channel
       </a>
       on May 26, 2009. The documentary, while not endorsing the movement, is described as giving the movement "more sympathetic, or less critical, airing than they've yet had (except among the converted)".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">
        <a href="#cite_note-124">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         124
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">
        <a href="#cite_note-125">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         125
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ul>

       <li id="cite_note-34">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-34">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation web">
          Buchanan, John.
          <a class="external text" href="http://web.archive.org/web/20040326051601/http://johnbuchanan.org/news/newsitem.php?section=INF&amp;id=1504&amp;showcat=4" rel="nofollow">
           "Is George Bush guilty of treason?"
          </a>
          . Archived from
          <a class="external text" href="http://johnbuchanan.org/news/newsitem.php?section=INF&amp;id=1504&amp;showcat=4" rel="nofollow">
           the original
          </a>
          on 2004-03-26
          <span class="reference-accessdate">
           . Retrieved
           <span class="nowrap">
            2011-09-19
           </span>
          </span>
          .
          <q>
           On September 1, 2000, before Mr. Bush took office, the Project for a New American Century proposed the invasions, without provocation or attack, of Afghanistan and Iraq. The motive? 'to protect America's oil interests.' The signatories to that sinister plan - Dick Cheney, Paul Wolfowitz, and Richard Perle, to name but a few  cleverly and dishonorably set the stage for all that would follow, including the horrifying spectacle of 9/11, when they noted that since well-fed and materially-comfortable Americans would lack the will and focus to fight such 'interventionist' wars - now known as 'The Bush Doctrine' - there must be a galvanizing incident on the order of Pearl Harbor.
          </q>
         </span>
